Second Refutation: The Miracle's Match to the Age's Excellence
The author presents the second refutation: the miracle is extraordinary and challengers are unable to oppose it in their own field.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument that miracles are of the type in which the challengers excel and thus their inability to oppose proves the miracle's authenticity.

Core Idea
Miracles match the expertise of the age to make the challenge undeniable.

The second detailed refutation focuses on the context of the miracle: it is not just any wonder, but one that directly challenges the experts of the time in their own field. By showing that the challengers are unable to produce anything similar despite their utmost motivation and ability, the miracle becomes a clear sign of divine endorsement.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read 'وثانياً: أن كلامنا فيما حصل الجزم بأنه خارق للعادة...' and note the conditions: the miracle must be definitely extraordinary and the challengers must be unable to oppose it.
Pay attention to the list of conditions.
2
Understand the principle of matching
Read the sentence about how each prophet's miracle was from the domain in which his people excelled (e.g., magic in Moses' time, medicine for Jesus, eloquence for Muhammad).
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: why does matching the expertise make the inability to oppose more significant?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : احتمال أن لا يكون خارقاً للعادة، بل ابتداء عادة أراد الله إجراءها أو تكرير عادة لا تكون إلا في دهور متطاولة، كعود الثوابت إلى نقطة معينة . الثالث : احتمال أن يكون مما يعارض إلا أنه لم يعارض لعدم بلوغه إلى من يقدر المعارضة، أو لمواضعة من القول، وموافقة في إعلاء كلمته، أو لخوف، أو لاستهانة وقلة مبالاة، أو لاشتغال بما هو أهم ، أو عورض ولم ينقل لمانع . الرابع : احتمال أن لا يكون لغرض التصديق، إما لانتفاء الغرض في فعله على ما هو المذهب، وإما لثبوت غرض آخر مثل ان يكون لطفاً بمكلف، أو إجابة لدعوته أو معجزة لنبي آخر أو ابتلاء للعبد لينال الثواب بالتوقف عن موجبه أو النظر والاجتهاد في دفعه كما في إنزال المتشابه أو إضلالاً للخلق على ما هو المذهب عندكم من أن الله يضل من يشاء من عباده، وبعدم تسليم انتفاء الاحتمالات، وكون المعجزة بمنزلة صريح القول من الله تعالى بأن المدعي صادق فهو لا يوجب صدقه إلا بعد استحالة الكذب في إخبار الله تعالى، ولا سبيل إلى ذلك بدليل السمع للزوم الدور، ولا بدليل العقل، لأن غايته أن الكذب قبيح، وهو على الله تعالى مستحيل، وثبوت المقدمتين بغير دليل السمع في حيز المنع . فالجواب إجمالاً أن الاحتمالات والتجويزات العقلية لا تنافي العلوم العادية الضرورية القطعية، فنحن نقطع بحصول العلم بالصدق عقيب ظهور المعجزة من غير التفات إلى ما ذكر من ! لا بالنفي ولا بالإثبات، كما يحصل في المثال المذكور، وإن كان الملك ظلوماً غشوماً كذوباً لا يبالي بإغواء رعيته والاستهزاء برسله، وتفصيلاً أولاً : أنا بينا أن لا مؤثر في الوجود إلا الله وحده ، سيما في مثل إحياء الموتى ، وانقلاب العصا حية، وانشقاق القمر، وسلام الحجر والمدر، على أن مجرد التمكين، وترك الدفع من قبل الحكيم القادر المختار كاف في إفادة المطلوب، ولهذا ذهب المعتزلة إلى ان المعجزة تكون فعلاً لله تعالى، أو واقعاً بأمره أو بتمكينه . وثانياً : أن كلامنا فيما حصل الجزم بأنه خارق للعادة، وأن المتحدين عجزوا عن معارضته مع كونهم أحق بها إن أمكنت لكثرة اشتغالهم بما يناسب ذلك، وكمالهم فيه وفرط اهتمامهم بالمعارضة ، وتوفر دواعيهم . ولهذا كانت معجزة كل نبي من جنس ما غلب على أهل زمانه وتهالكوا عليه وتفاخروا به، كالسحر في زمن موسى عليه السلام والطب في زمن عيسى والموسيقى في زمن داود والفصاحة في زمن محمد (صلى الله عليه وسلم). وثالثاً : أنه لا خفاء ولا خلاف في ترتيب الغايات والآثار على بعض أفعاله وإن لم يجعلها أغراضاً له على أنا لا نقول إنه فعل المعجزة لغرض التصديق، بل إنها دلت على تصديق من الله تعالى قائم بذاته سواء جعل من جنس العلم أو كلام النفس، أو غيرهما . ورابعاً: أن ظهور المعجزة على يد الكاذب لأي غرض فرض وإن جاز عقلاً بناء على شمول قدرة الله ، فهو ممتنع عادة معلوم الانتفاء، قطعاً، كما هو حكم سائر العاديات، وهذا ما قال القاضي: إن اقتران ظهور المعجزة بالصدق أحد العاديات، فإذا جوزنا انحرافها عن مجراها جاز إخلاء المعجزة عن اعتقاد الصدق، وحينئذ يجوز إظهاره على يد الكاذب، وإما بدون ذلك فلا ، لاستحالة العلم بصدق الكاذب، ومنا من قال باستحالته عقلاً، فالشيخ لافضائه إلى التعجيز عن إقامة الدلالة على صدق دعوى الرسالة، والإمام وكثير من المتكلمين، لأن الصدق مدلول بها لازم بمنزلة العلم لإتقان الفعل، فلو ظهرت من الكاذب، لزم كونه صادقاً كاذباً، وهو محال، والماتريدية لإيجابه المسوية بين الصادق والكاذب، وعدم التفرقة بين النبي والمتنبي، وهو سفه لا يليق بالحكيم . وخامساً: أن مجرد إظهار المعجزة على يده يفيدنا العلم بصدقة، وبتصديق الله إياه من غير افتقار إلى اعتبار كلام وإخبار، ومن هنا يصح التمسك بخبر النبي في إثبات الكلام، وامتناع الكذب والنقص على ما مر وإلى هذا يشير ما قال إمام الحرمين، أنا نجعل إظهار المعجزة تصديقاً بمنزلة أن يقول: جعلته رسولاً، وأنشأت الرسالة فيه كقولك : جعلتك وكيلاً، واستنبتك بشأن من غير قصد إلى
Second: the probability that it is not extraordinary but rather an initial custom that God willed to execute or a repetition of a custom that only occurs in long epochs, like the return of fixed stars to a specific point. Third: the probability that it is something that could be opposed but was not opposed due to not reaching one who can oppose it, or due to collusion in speech, agreement in elevating his word, or fear, or disdain and lack of concern, or preoccupation with what is more important, or it was opposed but not transmitted due to an impediment. Fourth: the probability that it is not for the purpose of verification, either because of the absence of purpose in His action according to the [Ash'ari] doctrine, or because of the existence of another purpose such as being a grace for a morally responsible person, or an answer to his supplication, or a miracle for another prophet, or a trial for the servant to attain reward by refraining from acting upon its implication or by examining and striving to rebut it, as in the revelation of ambiguous verses, or leading people astray according to your doctrine that God leads astray whom He wills of His servants, and by not conceding the negation of the probabilities, and that the miracle is like an explicit statement from God that the claimant is truthful, so it does not necessitate his truthfulness except after the impossibility of lying in God's reporting, and there is no way to that through transmitted evidence due to circularity, nor through reason, because at most lying is evil, and it is impossible for God, and establishing both premises without transmitted evidence is in the realm of denial. So the answer in summary: that probabilities and rational possibilities do not contradict necessary decisive ordinary knowledge; so we are certain of attaining knowledge of truthfulness upon the appearance of the miracle without paying attention to what was mentioned... neither by negation nor affirmation, as occurs in the mentioned example, even if the king is unjust, oppressive, deceitful, unconcerned with misleading his subjects and mocking his messengers. And in detail: First: we have shown that there is no effect in existence except God alone, especially in such things as reviving the dead, turning the staff into a snake, splitting the moon, and greeting of stones and clods, and that mere enabling and leaving off prevention from the Wise, Powerful, Free Agent is sufficient for producing the desired result, and for this the Mu'tazila held that the miracle is an act of God, or occurs by His command or by His enabling. Second: our discussion concerns what is determined to be extraordinary and that the challengers are unable to oppose it while they are most entitled to it if it were possible, due to their frequent occupation with what suits that, their perfection in it, their extreme concern for opposition, and their abundant motives. For this reason, the miracle of every prophet was of the kind that dominated the people of his time and upon which they fiercely competed and boasted, like magic in the time of Moses (peace be upon him), medicine in the time of Jesus, music in the time of David, and eloquence in the time of Muhammad (may God bless him and grant him peace). Third: there is no concealment nor disagreement regarding the ordering of ends and effects upon some of His actions even if He does not make them purposes for Himself, yet we do not say that He performed the miracle for the purpose of verification, but rather that it indicates a verification from God inherent in His essence, whether it is considered as knowledge or inner speech or otherwise. Fourth: the appearance of a miracle at the hand of a liar for any assumed purpose, even if rationally possible based on the comprehensiveness of God's power, is customarily impossible and known to be non-existent, certainly, just as is the case for all customary matters. This is what al-Qadi said: that the coupling of the appearance of the miracle with truthfulness is one of the customary things; if we permit its deviation from its course, it becomes permissible for the miracle to be devoid of belief in truthfulness, and then it is permissible for it to be shown at the hand of a liar. Otherwise, no, because of the impossibility of knowing the truthfulness of a liar. Among us, some have said it is rationally impossible: al-Shaykh [al-Ash'ari] because it leads to the inability to establish evidence for the truth of the claim of prophethood; al-Imam [al-Juwayni] and many theologians because truthfulness is implied by it as a necessary concomitant akin to knowledge due to the perfection of the act, so if it appeared from a liar, it would necessitate him being both truthful and lying, which is impossible; and the Maturidis because it necessitates equality between the truthful and the liar, and the lack of distinction between the prophet and the claimant to prophethood, which is foolishness unbefitting the Wise. Fifth: the mere appearance of the miracle at his hand provides us with knowledge of his truthfulness and of God's verification of him, without needing to consider speech or report. Hence, it is valid to rely on the prophet's report to establish speech, the impossibility of lying, and deficiency, as has passed. And to this refers what Imam al-Haramayn said: we make the appearance of the miracle a verification in the manner of saying: 'I have made him a messenger,' and the establishment of prophethood in him is like your saying: 'I have made you a deputy,' and I appointed you for a matter without intending to...
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This lengthy passage presents a series of objections (probabilities) against the conclusiveness of miracles as proofs of prophethood, followed by a summary response and five detailed refutations. The author begins by listing four possible objections: (1) The miracle might not be truly extraordinary but merely a rare custom initiated by God; (2) It might be open to opposition but was not opposed due to various reasons; (3) Its purpose might not be verification but something else; (4) Denial of the probabilities and the claim that a miracle is like an explicit statement from God, which only proves truth after establishing the impossibility of lying in God's reports—this cannot be proven by transmitted evidence (circular) nor reason. Then the summary answer: rational probabilities do not undermine necessary, certain, ordinary knowledge. We are certain of truth after a miracle just as we are certain in ordinary cases. Then five detailed answers: First, only God is the true agent, and His enabling alone suffices. Second, our discussion is about miracles that are known to be extraordinary and that the challengers are unable to oppose, with their strong motives. Miracles match the expertise of the age. Third, the miracle indicates divine verification inherently, not necessarily as a purpose. Fourth, a miracle at the hand of a liar is customarily impossible, and various opinions on its rational impossibility are discussed (Ash'ari, Juwayni, Maturidi). Fifth, the mere appearance of the miracle gives certain knowledge of truth without need for a verbal report. The passage ends with a quote from Imam al-Haramayn comparing the miracle to an explicit appointment.

Key Terms
خارق للعادة
معارضة
جنس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any miracle can be opposed by anyone; but the author argues that the inability of the experts themselves is key.
Correction: The miracle is designed to target the best in that field, so their failure is most telling.

Checkpoint
Why does the author mention that the miracle is from 'the kind that dominated the people of his time'?
A) To show that prophets were experts in that field.
B) To emphasize that the challengers are most competent to oppose it.
C) To indicate that miracles are only for certain times.
D) To prove that miracles are not necessary.

Key Takeaway
A miracle's conclusiveness is reinforced when it challenges the very experts who would naturally surpass it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The miracle of the Quran challenged the Arabs in their pride and joy: eloquence. What is the area of your life where you feel most competent and confident? If Allah were to challenge you there, would you be humble enough to recognize His sign, or would pride blind you? Commit to one specific way you will practice humility in that area this week.
?
The source says the challengers had 'abundant motives' (توفر دواعيهم) to oppose the miracle, yet they failed. Think of a truth you know from revelation—perhaps about prayer, charity, or character—that you have been resisting. What is the real motive behind your resistance? How can you surrender that area to Allah today?
?
Each prophet's miracle was perfectly matched to the people's expertise so that the proof was undeniable. Have you ever felt that Allah's guidance confronted you in a way that hit exactly where you were proud or comfortable? Describe that moment. What did you do? If you evaded, what step can you take now to finally respond to that call?

Miracles

Third and Fourth Refutations: Purpose and Customary Impossibility
The author gives the third and fourth detailed refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third argument (miracle indicates inherent divine verification) and the fourth argument (miracle at the hand of a liar is customarily impossible and rationally argued as impossible).

Core Idea
A miracle intrinsically shows God's verification, and its occurrence with a liar is impossible in practice and in reason.

The third and fourth refutations build on the first two. The third clarifies that the miracle itself indicates verification from God, regardless of purpose. The fourth tackles the most serious challenge: could a miracle happen to a liar? The author argues it is customarily impossible, and presents views from leading theologians that it is rationally impossible as well.

Guided Path
1
Read the third argument
Read 'وثالثاً: أنه لا خفاء ولا خلاف في ترتيب الغايات...' and note that the miracle indicates verification inherently, not as a purpose.
Contrast this with the objection that the miracle might have another purpose.
2
Read the fourth argument
Read 'ورابعاً: أن ظهور المعجزة على يد الكاذب...' and understand the concept of 'عاديات' (customary matters). The coupling of miracle with truth is customary.
Pay attention to the different opinions from al-Qadi, al-Ash'ari, al-Juwayni, and the Maturidis.
3
Contrast the two refutations
Notice that the third refutes the 'alternative purpose' objection, while the fourth refutes the possibility of miracle from a liar. They are distinct but complementary.

لاستحالة العلم بصدق الكاذب، ومنا من قال باستحالته عقلاً، فالشيخ لافضائه إلى التعجيز عن إقامة الدلالة على صدق دعوى الرسالة، والإمام وكثير من المتكلمين، لأن الصدق مدلول بها لازم بمنزلة العلم لإتقان الفعل، فلو ظهرت من الكاذب، لزم كونه صادقاً كاذباً، وهو محال، والماتريدية لإيجابه المسوية بين الصادق والكاذب، وعدم التفرقة بين النبي والمتنبي، وهو سفه لا يليق بالحكيم . وخامساً: أن مجرد إظهار المعجزة على يده يفيدنا العلم بصدقة، وبتصديق الله إياه من غير افتقار إلى اعتبار كلام وإخبار، ومن هنا يصح التمسك بخبر النبي في إثبات الكلام، وامتناع الكذب والنقص على ما مر وإلى هذا يشير ما قال إمام الحرمين، أنا نجعل إظهار المعجزة تصديقاً بمنزلة أن يقول: جعلته رسولاً، وأنشأت الرسالة فيه كقولك : جعلتك وكيلاً، واستنبتك بشأن من غير قصد إلى
Second: the probability that it is not extraordinary but rather an initial custom that God willed to execute or a repetition of a custom that only occurs in long epochs, like the return of fixed stars to a specific point. Third: the probability that it is something that could be opposed but was not opposed due to not reaching one who can oppose it, or due to collusion in speech, agreement in elevating his word, or fear, or disdain and lack of concern, or preoccupation with what is more important, or it was opposed but not transmitted due to an impediment. Fourth: the probability that it is not for the purpose of verification, either because of the absence of purpose in His action according to the [Ash'ari] doctrine, or because of the existence of another purpose such as being a grace for a morally responsible person, or an answer to his supplication, or a miracle for another prophet, or a trial for the servant to attain reward by refraining from acting upon its implication or by examining and striving to rebut it, as in the revelation of ambiguous verses, or leading people astray according to your doctrine that God leads astray whom He wills of His servants, and by not conceding the negation of the probabilities, and that the miracle is like an explicit statement from God that the claimant is truthful, so it does not necessitate his truthfulness except after the impossibility of lying in God's reporting, and there is no way to that through transmitted evidence due to circularity, nor through reason, because at most lying is evil, and it is impossible for God, and establishing both premises without transmitted evidence is in the realm of denial. So the answer in summary: that probabilities and rational possibilities do not contradict necessary decisive ordinary knowledge; so we are certain of attaining knowledge of truthfulness upon the appearance of the miracle without paying attention to what was mentioned... neither by negation nor affirmation, as occurs in the mentioned example, even if the king is unjust, oppressive, deceitful, unconcerned with misleading his subjects and mocking his messengers. And in detail: First: we have shown that there is no effect in existence except God alone, especially in such things as reviving the dead, turning the staff into a snake, splitting the moon, and greeting of stones and clods, and that mere enabling and leaving off prevention from the Wise, Powerful, Free Agent is sufficient for producing the desired result, and for this the Mu'tazila held that the miracle is an act of God, or occurs by His command or by His enabling. Second: our discussion concerns what is determined to be extraordinary and that the challengers are unable to oppose it while they are most entitled to it if it were possible, due to their frequent occupation with what suits that, their perfection in it, their extreme concern for opposition, and their abundant motives. For this reason, the miracle of every prophet was of the kind that dominated the people of his time and upon which they fiercely competed and boasted, like magic in the time of Moses (peace be upon him), medicine in the time of Jesus, music in the time of David, and eloquence in the time of Muhammad (may God bless him and grant him peace). Third: there is no concealment nor disagreement regarding the ordering of ends and effects upon some of His actions even if He does not make them purposes for Himself, yet we do not say that He performed the miracle for the purpose of verification, but rather that it indicates a verification from God inherent in His essence, whether it is considered as knowledge or inner speech or otherwise. Fourth: the appearance of a miracle at the hand of a liar for any assumed purpose, even if rationally possible based on the comprehensiveness of God's power, is customarily impossible and known to be non-existent, certainly, just as is the case for all customary matters. This is what al-Qadi said: that the coupling of the appearance of the miracle with truthfulness is one of the customary things; if we permit its deviation from its course, it becomes permissible for the miracle to be devoid of belief in truthfulness, and then it is permissible for it to be shown at the hand of a liar. Otherwise, no, because of the impossibility of knowing the truthfulness of a liar. Among us, some have said it is rationally impossible: al-Shaykh [al-Ash'ari] because it leads to the inability to establish evidence for the truth of the claim of prophethood; al-Imam [al-Juwayni] and many theologians because truthfulness is implied by it as a necessary concomitant akin to knowledge due to the perfection of the act, so if it appeared from a liar, it would necessitate him being both truthful and lying, which is impossible; and the Maturidis because it necessitates equality between the truthful and the liar, and the lack of distinction between the prophet and the claimant to prophethood, which is foolishness unbefitting the Wise. Fifth: the mere appearance of the miracle at his hand provides us with knowledge of his truthfulness and of God's verification of him, without needing to consider speech or report. Hence, it is valid to rely on the prophet's report to establish speech, the impossibility of lying, and deficiency, as has passed. And to this refers what Imam al-Haramayn said: we make the appearance of the miracle a verification in the manner of saying: 'I have made him a messenger,' and the establishment of prophethood in him is like your saying: 'I have made you a deputy,' and I appointed you for a matter without intending to...
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This lengthy passage presents a series of objections (probabilities) against the conclusiveness of miracles as proofs of prophethood, followed by a summary response and five detailed refutations. The author begins by listing four possible objections: (1) The miracle might not be truly extraordinary but merely a rare custom initiated by God; (2) It might be open to opposition but was not opposed due to various reasons; (3) Its purpose might not be verification but something else; (4) Denial of the probabilities and the claim that a miracle is like an explicit statement from God, which only proves truth after establishing the impossibility of lying in God's reports—this cannot be proven by transmitted evidence (circular) nor reason. Then the summary answer: rational probabilities do not undermine necessary, certain, ordinary knowledge. We are certain of truth after a miracle just as we are certain in ordinary cases. Then five detailed answers: First, only God is the true agent, and His enabling alone suffices. Second, our discussion is about miracles that are known to be extraordinary and that the challengers are unable to oppose, with their strong motives. Miracles match the expertise of the age. Third, the miracle indicates divine verification inherently, not necessarily as a purpose. Fourth, a miracle at the hand of a liar is customarily impossible, and various opinions on its rational impossibility are discussed (Ash'ari, Juwayni, Maturidi). Fifth, the mere appearance of the miracle gives certain knowledge of truth without need for a verbal report. The passage ends with a quote from Imam al-Haramayn comparing the miracle to an explicit appointment.

Key Terms
غرض
عاديات
متنبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God is all-powerful, He could give a miracle to a liar, so miracles aren't proof.
Correction: The author argues it is customarily impossible and rationally impossible for various reasons.

Checkpoint
What is the main basis of al-Juwayni's argument against a miracle for a liar?
A) It would lead to the inability to prove prophecy.
B) It would necessitate the liar being both truthful and lying.
C) It would make God foolish.
D) It goes against the custom of prophets.

Key Takeaway
The third and fourth refutations show that a miracle is inherently tied to truth and that its occurrence with a liar is both customarily and rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the appearance of a miracle with a liar is impossible because it would destroy the very purpose of prophethood, how do you know that your own faith in the Prophet ﷺ is not based on a deception? What in your heart witnesses to the truth of the message beyond intellectual proofs?
?
The third refutation says the miracle itself is the verification from God, not a separate act. When you read the Quran or reflect on the Prophet's life, do you sense that inherent verification? Or are you waiting for an external sign? What would change in your life if you truly believed that the miracle is already speaking directly to your soul?
?
The Maturidis argue that if miracles could appear with liars, there would be no distinction between a true prophet and a false claimant. But in your daily life, how do you distinguish truth from falsehood in matters of faith? Are you relying on clear signs from God, or are you being swayed by impressive speech and worldly charisma?

Fifth Refutation: Direct Knowledge from the Miracle's Appearance
The author presents the fifth refutation: the miracle gives direct knowledge of truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth and final argument: the mere appearance of the miracle gives us direct knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness without need for a verbal report from God.

Core Idea
The miracle itself is the divine speech; no further statement is needed.

The fifth refutation concludes the detailed responses by asserting that the miracle itself provides immediate knowledge of truthfulness. It is like God saying 'I have made him a messenger' directly. This argument connects to earlier discussions about divine speech and the impossibility of deception.

Guided Path
1
Read the fifth argument
Read 'وخامساً: أن مجرد إظهار المعجزة على يده يفيدنا العلم بصدقة...' and note that knowledge comes directly from the miracle, not from a separate statement.
2
Understand the analogy
Read the quote from Imam al-Haramayn comparing the miracle to an explicit appointment: 'جعلته رسولاً'.
3
Connect to earlier topics
The text mentions that this is why we can rely on the prophet's report to establish divine speech. Reflect on how this closes the argument.

بالإثبات، كما يحصل في المثال المذكور، وإن كان الملك ظلوماً غشوماً كذوباً لا يبالي بإغواء رعيته والاستهزاء برسله، وتفصيلاً أولاً : أنا بينا أن لا مؤثر في الوجود إلا الله وحده ، سيما في مثل إحياء الموتى ، وانقلاب العصا حية، وانشقاق القمر، وسلام الحجر والمدر، على أن مجرد التمكين، وترك الدفع من قبل الحكيم القادر المختار كاف في إفادة المطلوب، ولهذا ذهب المعتزلة إلى ان المعجزة تكون فعلاً لله تعالى، أو واقعاً بأمره أو بتمكينه . وثانياً : أن كلامنا فيما حصل الجزم بأنه خارق للعادة، وأن المتحدين عجزوا عن معارضته مع كونهم أحق بها إن أمكنت لكثرة اشتغالهم بما يناسب ذلك، وكمالهم فيه وفرط اهتمامهم بالمعارضة عليه وسلم). وثالثاً : أنه لا خفاء ولا خلاف في ترتيب الغايات والآثار على بعض أفعاله وإن لم يجعلها أغراضاً له على أنا لا نقول إنه فعل المعجزة لغرض التصديق، بل إنها دلت على تصديق من الله تعالى قائم بذاته سواء جعل من جنس العلم أو كلام النفس، أو غيرهما . ورابعاً: أن ظهور المعجزة على يد الكاذب لأي غرض فرض وإن جاز عقلاً بناء على شمول قدرة الله ، فهو ممتنع عادة معلوم الانتفاء، قطعاً، كما هو حكم سائر العاديات، وهذا ما قال القاضي: إن اقتران ظهور المعجزة بالصدق أحد العاديات، فإذا جوزنا انحرافها عن مجراها جاز إخلاء المعجزة عن اعتقاد الصدق، وحينئذ يجوز إظهاره على يد الكاذب، وإما بدون ذلك فلا ، لاستحالة العلم بصدق الكاذب، ومنا من قال باستحالته عقلاً، فالشيخ لافضائه إلى التعجيز عن إقامة الدلالة على صدق دعوى الرسالة، والإمام وكثير من المتكلمين، لأن الصدق مدلول بها لازم بمنزلة العلم لإتقان الفعل، فلو ظهرت من الكاذب، لزم كونه صادقاً كاذباً، وهو محال، والماتريدية لإيجابه المسوية بين الصادق والكاذب، وعدم التفرقة بين النبي والمتنبي، وهو سفه لا يليق بالحكيم . وخامساً: أن مجرد إظهار المعجزة على يده يفيدنا العلم بصدقة، وبتصديق الله إياه من غير افتقار إلى اعتبار كلام وإخبار، ومن هنا يصح التمسك بخبر النبي في إثبات الكلام، وامتناع الكذب والنقص على ما مر وإلى هذا يشير ما قال إمام الحرمين، أنا Second: the probability that it is not extraordinary but rather an initial custom that God willed to execute or a repetition of a custom that only occurs in long epochs, like the return of fixed stars to a specific point. Third: the probability that it is something that could be opposed but was not opposed due to not reaching one who can oppose it, or due to collusion in speech, agreement in elevating his word, or fear, or disdain and lack of concern, or preoccupation with what is more important, or it was opposed but not transmitted due to an impediment. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that we need an explicit divine statement to know a prophet is truthful; the miracle itself is that statement.

According to the fifth argument, what does the mere appearance of the miracle provide?
A) A probable indication

C) A basis for requiring additional proof

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Miracles
intermediate

Knowledge of the Unseen as a Miracle
The author explains the first type of miracle: knowledge of the unseen via soul's connection to high principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author explains the possibility of prophets knowing the unseen through the soul's connection to higher principles.

Core Idea
Knowledge of the unseen arises from the soul's connection to the intellects, like a mirror facing the sun.

This passage dives into the first category of miracles: knowledge of the unseen. The author argues that just as ordinary people glimpse the future in dreams, prophets and saints can access hidden knowledge through their soul's link to the celestial realm. This is not a random gift but a natural preparedness.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage for the first type of miracle once, then its literal translation. Let the author's argument unfold.
Notice the analogy with sleep and the concept of 'connection'.
2
Identify the analogy and the cause
Find the analogy with dreams and the stated cause: the soul's connection to the high principles (intellects and celestial souls).
The cause is described as 'soul's connection' (ittiṣāl al-nafs).
3
Understand the mechanism and preparedness
Note how the author explains the universal knowledge of intellects vs. particular knowledge of the perfect ones, and the role of preparedness.
The mirror analogy illustrates that the soul must be ready to receive knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تقريرهم من المعجزات فإجمالاً أنه لا يبعد أن يختص بعض النفوس الإنسانية بقوة هي مبدأ لأفعال غريبة بسبب ما لها من الخصوصية الشخصية، أو بسبب أمر طاريء عليها من غير اكتساب أو حاصل لها بالاكتساب على ما هو شأن أكثر الأولياء ، وهذا لا ينافي اتحاد النفوس بحسب النوع : وتفصيلاً أن المشهور من معجزات الأنبياء وكرامات الأولياء ثلاث بحسب القوة الإنسانية، والقوة الحيوانية باعتبار الحركات والسكنات .

فالأول : الاطلاع على المغيبات، وليس ببعيد لتحقيقه في حال النوم على ما تعرفه من نفسك وتسمعه من غيرك. وسبب ذلك اتصال النفس بالمبادىء العالية اعني العقول والنفوس السماوية المنتقشة بصور ما يستند إليها من الحوادث لما تقرر من أنها عالمة بذواتها، وأن العلم بالعلل والأسباب يوجب العلم بالمعلولات والمسببات. غاية الأمر أن علم العقول بالحوادث لا يكون إلا على وجه كلي خال من قيد الهذية وخصوص الوقتية ، والكاملون قد يدركونها على الوجه الجزئي، إما بجعلها جزئية بمعونة الحواس الباطنة على ما قررها الحكماء، وإما لارتسامها في النفوس السماوية، كذلك على ما يراه بعضهم، ومعنى اتصال النفس بالمبادىء العالية صيرورتها مستعدة لفيضان العلوم عليها بحصول القوى لها وزوال المانع ، أعني الشواغل الحسية عنها، بمنزلة مرآة مجلوة تحاذي شطر الشمس، ولا يلزم من ذلك انتقاشها بجميع ما في المبادىء من الصور، لأن لقبول كل صورة استعداداً يخصها .

والثاني : ظهور حركات وأفعال تعجز عن أمثالها أمثاله كحدوث رياح وزلازل، وحرق وغرق، وهلاك أشخاص ظالمة، وخراب مدن فاسدة وانفجار المياه من الأحجار، بل من الأصابع، وليس ببعيد، لأن علاقة النفس مع البدن إنما بالتدبير والتصرف لا الحلول (۱) والانطباع ، فيجوز أن يكون بعض النفوس هي

(۱) الحلول السرياني: عبارة عن اتحاد الجسمين بحيث تكون الإشارة إلى أحدهما إشارة إلى الآخر، -
As for their detailed account of miracles in summary: it is not improbable that some human souls are distinguished by a power that is the principle of strange actions due to their personal particularity, or due to an accidental matter upon them without acquisition, or obtained by acquisition as is the case with most saints (awliyā'). This does not contradict the unity of souls in species. In detail: the well-known among the miracles of prophets and the wonders of saints are three, according to the human power and the animal power with respect to motion and stillness. The first: knowledge of unseen things. This is not far-fetched, as its realization is seen in sleep as you know from yourself and hear from others. The cause of that is the soul's connection to the high principles, namely the intellects (ʿuqūl) and celestial souls (nufūs samāwiyya) which are impressed with the images of events that depend on them, since it is established that they are knowledgeable by their essences, and that knowledge of causes necessitates knowledge of effects. The only difference is that the knowledge of the intellects regarding events is only in a universal manner, free from the condition of 'thisness' and temporal particularity. The perfect ones may perceive them in a particular manner, either by making them particular with the aid of the inner senses (al-ḥawāss al-bāṭina) as the philosophers have established, or because they are imprinted in the celestial souls accordingly, as some hold. And the meaning of the soul's connection to the high principles is that it becomes prepared for the emanation of sciences upon it by acquiring powers and removing the obstacle, namely the sensory distractions from it, like a polished mirror facing the sun. It does not follow from this that it becomes impressed with all the images in the principles, because for accepting each image there is a specific preparedness. The second: the occurrence of motions and acts that others like him are incapable of, such as the occurrence of winds and earthquakes, burning and drowning, destruction of oppressive persons, ruin of corrupt cities, springing forth of water from rocks, even from fingers. This is not far-fetched, because the relationship of the soul to the body is only by management and disposal, not by indwelling (ḥulūl) and impression. So it is possible that some souls are (the principle of such acts). (Footnote) al-ḥulūl al-siryānī: it is an expression for the union of two bodies such that pointing to one of them is pointing to the other.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed analysis of miracles, first in summary and then in detail. The author states that it is not improbable for certain souls to be endowed with a power producing extraordinary acts, which may be inherent, accidental, or acquired (as with saints). This does not contradict the unity of human souls in species. Then he enumerates three well-known types of miracles based on the human (rational) and animal (sensory-motor) powers. The first type is knowledge of the unseen. The author argues this is plausible by analogy with dreams, where ordinary people gain knowledge of future events. The cause is the soul's connection to the high principles (intellects and celestial souls) which contain the forms of all events. Since these principles know themselves and their effects, knowledge of causes yields knowledge of effects. The intellects know events universally; the perfect ones perceive them particularly via inner senses or imprinting in celestial souls. The soul's connection means it becomes receptive to emanation of sciences, like a polished mirror facing the sun, but it does not automatically receive all images due to differing preparedness. The second type is extraordinary physical acts like causing winds, earthquakes, burning, drowning, etc. The author explains this by the soul's relation to the body: the soul manages and disposes the body without indwelling (ḥulūl). Therefore, a powerful soul can affect external matter similarly, producing marvels. The footnote defines 'ḥulūl' as the union of two bodies such that pointing to one points to the other.

استعداد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That knowledge of the future by prophets is direct revelation without any natural cause or preparedness.
Correction: The passage explains that such knowledge results from the soul's connection to higher principles, requiring preparedness and removal of sensory distractions.

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the cause of a prophet's knowledge of unseen future events?
A) Direct revelation from God without any mediation.
B) The connection of his soul to the high principles.
C) His physical senses.
D) The challenge of others.

Key Takeaway
The soul's connection to the high principles enables knowledge of the unseen, but this requires specific preparedness and removal of sensory distractions.

?
The perfect ones attained knowledge of the unseen through preparedness and connection. Are you actively polishing your soul's mirror, or are you content with spiritual stagnation? What specific practice will you adopt this week to connect more deeply?
?
When you face an uncertain future, do you turn to the source of all knowledge (the High Principles) through reflection and supplication, or do you rely solely on your own calculations? How can you strengthen that connection tonight?

Extraordinary Physical Acts as Miracles
The author explains the second type of miracle: extraordinary physical acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's explanation of extraordinary physical acts as miracles through the soul's relation to the body.

Core Idea
Extraordinary physical acts are possible because the soul manages the body without indwelling.

The second type of miracle involves physical acts beyond normal human capacity, such as causing winds, earthquakes, or water from rocks. The author grounds this in the soul's relationship to the body: the soul is not within the body but manages it externally, so a powerful soul can directly affect external matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage for the second type of miracle, then its literal translation. Note the list of examples.
The passage ends mid-sentence; focus on the part that is present.
2
Identify the examples of extraordinary acts
List the examples given: winds, earthquakes, burning, drowning, destruction of oppressive people, water from rocks and fingers.
3
Analyze the causal explanation
Understand the author's reasoning: because the soul relates to the body by management (tadbīr) and disposal, not by indwelling (ḥulūl), a strong soul can affect external matter directly.
The footnote defines ḥulūl as the union of two bodies, which is not the case for soul and body.

First Type of Miracles: Knowledge of the Unseen
Taftazani introduces miracles and explains the first type: knowledge of the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Taftazani's explanation of knowledge of the unseen as the first type of miracle, its cause through the soul's connection to higher principles, and the analogy of the polished mirror.

Core Idea
Knowledge of the unseen is possible through the soul's connection to higher intellects, like a mirror to the sun.

Taftazani begins his discussion of miracles by first giving a general summary and then detailing three types. The first type is knowledge of the unseen. He argues that this is not only possible for prophets and saints but even occurs in ordinary dreams. In this lesson, we will explore the cause of such knowledge and the philosophical framework behind it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation to get a sense of the argument.
Notice the shift from summary (ijmal) to detail (tafsil).
2
Understand the summary and classification
Identify the general claim about souls and the three types of miracles based on human and animal powers.
The first type is the focus of this lesson.
3
Identify the cause of knowledge of the unseen
Find the cause: 'soul's connection with the high principles' (i.e., intellects and celestial souls). Understand how this enables knowledge.
The cause is explained through the nature of the principles being knowing and the chain of causes.
4
Grasp the analogy of the polished mirror
Understand the comparison: the soul becomes like a polished mirror facing the sun, ready to receive knowledge when sensory distractions are removed.
The analogy emphasizes preparedness and removal of obstacles.
5
Reflect on the condition of specific preparedness
Note that not all images are received; each requires a specific preparedness, explaining why not everyone has such knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تقريرهم من المعجزات فإجمالاً أنه لا يبعد أن يختص بعض النفوس الإنسانية بقوة هي مبدأ لأفعال غريبة بسبب ما لها من الخصوصية الشخصية، أو بسبب أمر طاريء عليها من غير اكتساب أو حاصل لها بالاكتساب على ما هو شأن أكثر الأولياء ، وهذا لا ينافي اتحاد النفوس بحسب النوع : وتفصيلاً أن المشهور من معجزات الأنبياء وكرامات الأولياء ثلاث بحسب القوة الإنسانية، والقوة الحيوانية باعتبار الحركات والسكنات . فالأول : الاطلاع على المغيبات، وليس ببعيد لتحقيقه في حال النوم على ما تعرفه من نفسك وتسمعه من غيرك. وسبب ذلك اتصال النفس بالمبادىء العالية اعني العقول والنفوس السماوية المنتقشة بصور ما يستند إليها من الحوادث لما تقرر من أنها عالمة بذواتها، وأن العلم بالعلل والأسباب يوجب العلم بالمعلولات والمسببات. غاية الأمر أن علم العقول بالحوادث لا يكون إلا على وجه كلي خال من قيد الهذية وخصوص الوقتية ، والكاملون قد يدركونها على الوجه الجزئي، إما بجعلها جزئية بمعونة الحواس الباطنة على ما قررها الحكماء، وإما لارتسامها في النفوس السماوية، كذلك على ما يراه بعضهم، ومعنى اتصال النفس بالمبادىء العالية صيرورتها مستعدة لفيضان العلوم عليها بحصول القوى لها وزوال المانع ، أعني الشواغل الحسية عنها، بمنزلة مرآة مجلوة تحاذي شطر الشمس، ولا يلزم من ذلك انتقاشها بجميع ما في المبادىء من الصور، لأن لقبول كل صورة استعداداً يخصها.
As for their establishment from miracles: in summary, it is not unlikely that some human souls are distinguished by a power that is a source of strange acts, due to their personal particularity, or due to an accidental matter without acquisition, or acquired by them through acquisition as is the case with most saints. And this does not contradict the unity of souls in species. And in detail: the well-known miracles of prophets and marvels of saints are three according to the human power and the animal power with respect to movements and states. The first: knowledge of the unseen, and it is not far-fetched due to its realization in sleep, as you know from yourself and hear from others. The cause of that is the soul's connection with the high principles, namely the intellects and celestial souls which are impressed with images of events that proceed from them, since it is established that they are knowing in themselves, and that knowledge of causes necessitates knowledge of effects. The only thing is that the intellects' knowledge of events is only universal, free of the condition of 'this-ness' and temporal particularity. The perfect ones may perceive them in a particular manner, either by making them particular with the help of the internal senses as the philosophers have established, or due to their being imprinted in the celestial souls as some hold. The meaning of the soul's connection with the high principles is that it becomes prepared for the emanation of knowledge upon it by acquiring powers and removal of the obstacle, i.e., sensory distractions from it, like a polished mirror facing the direction of the sun. And it does not follow from that that it is impressed with all images in the principles, because for accepting each image there is a specific preparedness.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a demonstration and classification of miracles. It begins with a general summary: miracles are not impossible because human souls can possess extraordinary powers, either inherently or through acquisition, without contradicting the unity of the human species. It then provides a detailed enumeration of three types of miraculous events, based on the human power and the animal power. The first type is knowledge of the unseen (al-ittila' 'ala al-mughayyabat). The author argues that this is not far-fetched because it occurs in dreams, which is a common experience. The cause is the soul's connection (ittisal) with the high principles (al-mabadi' al-'aliya), i.e., the intellects and celestial souls that contain the forms of all events. Since these principles know themselves, they know their effects. However, their knowledge is universal; perfect individuals can perceive particular instances either through the internal senses or through the imprint in celestial souls. This connection is compared to a polished mirror facing the sun, and readiness depends on preparedness; not all images are received, only those for which there is specific capacity.

Miracles
beginner

Second Type of Miracles: Extraordinary Movements and Actions
Taftazani explains the second type of miracles: extraordinary physical phenomena.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the soul's relationship to the body as management and disposal (not indwelling) makes extraordinary physical miracles possible.

Core Idea
The soul governs bodies by management, not by dwelling inside.

Taftazani now turns to the second category of miracles: extraordinary physical events like storms, earthquakes, or water flowing from stones. He argues that such events are rational because the soul does not need to inhabit a body to affect it; it manages from its own body. This opens the door to souls influencing external elements.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold.
The passage includes a footnote on two types of hulul; note its role.
2
Identify the examples of extraordinary actions
List the examples given: winds, earthquakes, burning, drowning, destruction of tyrants, ruin of cities, water from stones/fingers.
These are beyond normal human capacity.
3
Understand the key principle
Notice that the soul's relation to the body is defined as 'management and disposal' (tadbīr wa taṣarruf), not indwelling (ḥulūl) or impression (inṭibā‘).
This is the logical basis for the possibility.
4
Analyze how this principle supports the possibility
Because the soul is not physically tied to its body, it can potentially influence other bodies, even the whole elemental world.
A powerful soul becomes like the soul of the world of elements.
5
Review the footnote on indwelling
Read the two distinctions: permeating indwelling (ḥulūl siryānī) and container indwelling (ḥulūl jiwārī). Understand that neither applies to the soul-body relation.
This prevents a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني : ظهور حركات وأفعال تعجز عن أمثالها أمثاله كحدوث رياح وزلازل، وحرق وغرق، وهلاك أشخاص ظالمة، وخراب مدن فاسدة وانفجار المياه من الأحجار، بل من الأصابع، وليس ببعيد، لأن علاقة النفس مع البدن إنما بالتدبير والتصرف لا الحلول (۱) والانطباع ، فيجوز أن يكون بعض النفوس من القوة بحيث يتصرف في أجسام أخر غير بدنها، بل في كلية العناصر، حتى كأنها نفس لعالم العناصر. (۱) الحلول السرياني: عبارة عن اتحاد الجسمين بحيث تكون الإشارة إلى أحدهما إشارة إلى الآخر، كحلول ماء الورد في الورد فيسمى الساري حالاً، والمسرى فيه محلاً. الحلول الجواري: عبارة عن كون أحد الجسمين ظرفاً للآخر كحلول الماء في الكوز.
And the second: the appearance of movements and actions that are beyond the capacity of their likes, such as the occurrence of winds and earthquakes, burning and drowning, destruction of tyrannical individuals, ruin of corrupt cities, and gushing of water from stones, even from fingers. And it is not far-fetched, because the relationship of the soul with the body is only by management and disposal, not by indwelling (hulul) or impression. So it is possible that some souls are of such power that they dispose of other bodies besides their own, indeed in the whole of the elements, such that it is as if they are the soul of the world of elements. (1) al-Hulul al-siryanī: it is the union of two bodies such that pointing to one is pointing to the other, like the indwelling of rose water in the rose; the permeating is called the indweller and the permeated is the place. al-Hulul al-jawārī: it is that one body is a container for the other, like water in a jug.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of miracles: extraordinary movements and actions (zuhūr ḥarakāt wa af‘āl) that are beyond the capacity of ordinary humans, such as natural disasters or wonders like water gushing from stones or fingers. The author argues this is not far-fetched because the soul's relation to the body is one of management and disposal (tadbīr wa taṣarruf), not indwelling or impression (ḥulūl wa inṭibā‘). Therefore, a powerful soul can affect other bodies, even all the elements, as if it were the soul of the elemental world. The footnote clarifies two types of indwelling: permeating indwelling (ḥulūl siryānī) like rose water in a rose, and container indwelling (ḥulūl jiwārī) like water in a jug. The passage thus uses the denial of ḥulūl to allow for the soul's independent influence.

Key Terms
ظهور حركات وأفعال
الحلول السرياني
الحلول الجواري
التدبير والتصرف
الانطباع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That miracles of this type require the soul to physically inhabit or mix with the affected bodies.
Correction: The author clarifies that the soul only manages and disposes, not indwells or impresses.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say it is possible for a powerful soul to affect other bodies?
A) Because the soul can physically leave its body
B) Because the soul's relation to the body is management, not indwelling
C) Because the soul is a physical substance
D) Because the soul is present in all bodies

Key Takeaway
Extraordinary physical miracles are possible because the soul governs bodies by management, not by physical indwelling.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if your soul is confined to your body, or do you truly believe it can influence the world around you? When have you seen the effect of a righteous person's soul on their environment? How does that challenge your daily habits?
?
If the soul manages without indwelling, then your connection to Allah is not limited by physical distance. Are you relying on physical rituals alone, or are you cultivating the inner power of your soul to manage your life and affect others?
?
The passage says a powerful soul can become 'as if it is the soul of the world of elements.' Imagine if you truly harnessed your soul's God-given management. What would change in how you interact with people, nature, and even your own problems? Are you content with a powerless perception of your soul?

The Third Type of Miracles: Prolonged Abstention from Food
Taftazani explains the third type of miracles: prolonged abstention from food.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Taftazani justifies the possibility of prolonged abstention from food as a miracle and why it is more fitting for gnostics than for the sick.

Core Idea
Prolonged abstention from food can be a miracle arising from spiritual mastery, not merely illness.

Taftazani continues his discussion of miracles by presenting the third type: the ability to go without food for an extended period. He argues that this is not far-fetched, drawing an analogy with illness and then showing how it is even more appropriate for perfect individuals whose souls dominate their bodies. This lesson will examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand the overall argument.
Notice the three reasons given in the text.
2
Identify the main argument and three reasons
The author first establishes the possibility by analogy to illness, then asserts it is more fitting for gnostics. Identify the three reasons he lists for this greater fittingness.
The reasons are enumerated in Arabic: 'أما أولاً... أما ثانياً... أما ثالثاً'
3
Reflect on the comparison
Consider how this type of miracle differs from ordinary illness. Why does the author consider it a miracle rather than a pathology?
Think about the role of the soul's dominance over bodily powers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث: الإمساك عن القوت مدة غير معتادة، وليس ببعيد كما في بعض الأمراض لاشتغال الطبيعة بهضم الأخلاط الفاسدة، وتحليل المواد الردية عن تحليل المواد المحمودة والرطوبات الأصلية المحوج إلى البدل، فيجوز في حق الأشخاص الكاملة لانجذاب نفوسهم إلى جناب القدس بالكلية، واستتباعها القوى الجسمانية التي بها الهضم والشهوة والتغذية وما يتعلق بذلك، بل لا يبعد أن يكون هذا من حق هؤلاء أولى وأقرب منه في المرض لكون احتياج المريض إلى الغذاء أوفر وأوفى أما أولاً فلتحلل رطوباته بسبب الحرارة الغريبة المسماة بسوء المزاج ) . وأما ثانياً فلفرط احتياجه إلى حفظ القوى البدنية بحفظ الرطوبات التي بها تعتدل الحرارة الغريزية، وذلك لما عرض لها بسبب المرض المضاد لها من الفتور. وأما ثالثاً فلاختصاص العارف بأمر يقتضي الاستغناء الغذاء، وهو السكون البدني الحاصل بسبب ترك القوى البدنية أفاعيلها عند متابعتها النفس. (۱) في (ب) أكثر بدلاً من (أوفى). (۲) المزاج : كيفية متشابهة تحصل عن تفاعل عناصر منافرة لأجزاء مماسة بحيث تكسر سورة كل منها سورة كيفية الآخر.
And the third: abstention from sustenance for an unusual period, and it is not far-fetched, as in some illnesses when nature is occupied with digesting corrupt humors and analyzing bad materials, preventing analysis of praiseworthy materials and original moistures that require replacement. So it is permissible for perfect individuals because their souls are drawn completely to the Holy Presence, and they subjugate the bodily powers responsible for digestion, appetite, nutrition, and what pertains to that. Rather, it is not far that this is more fitting and closer to them than to the sick, since the sick person’s need for food is more abundant and more complete. First: because his moistures dissolve due to the alien heat called bad temperament (sū’ al-mizāj). Second: because of his extreme need to preserve bodily powers by preserving the moistures that balance the innate heat, due to the weakness that affects them because of the opposing disease. Third: because the gnostic (al-‘ārif) is distinguished by a matter that necessitates independence from food, namely bodily stillness (sukūn badānī) resulting from the bodily powers abandoning their actions when they follow the soul. (1) In copy (b): 'akthar' instead of 'awfā'. (2) al-Mizāj: a similar quality resulting from the interaction of opposing elements in contiguous parts such that the force of each breaks the force of the other's quality.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage presents the third type of miracles: prolonged abstention from food. The author first argues it is not far-fetched, citing analogies from illness where nature is preoccupied with corrupt humors, reducing the need for food. Then he asserts it is even more fitting for perfect individuals (like saints) because their souls are completely attracted to the Holy Presence, subjugating bodily powers. He gives three reasons why this abstention is more appropriate for them than for the sick: (1) the sick have dissolving moistures and bad temperament; (2) the sick need to preserve body powers; (3) the gnostic (al-‘ārif) has bodily stillness as bodily powers cease actions when following the soul. The passage includes a textual variant note (1) and a definition of mizāj (temperament) as a quality arising from elemental interaction.

Key Terms
الإمساك عن القوت
الأخلاط الفاسدة
سوء المزاج
السكون البدني
العارف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prolonged abstention from food is only possible through direct divine intervention or is always a sign of illness.
Correction: The author shows it can result from spiritual mastery, where the soul's dominance over bodily powers reduces the need for food, making it a miracle distinct from illness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, one reason abstention from food is more fitting for the gnostic than the sick is:
A) The gnostic has more abundant food
B) The gnostic experiences bodily stillness from following the soul
C) The sick have better digestion
D) The gnostic consumes less moisture

Key Takeaway
Prolonged abstention from food can be a miracle when it occurs due to spiritual mastery, and it differs from illness-related abstention in its cause and fittingness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel physical hunger, does it often overpower your spiritual focus? What one change could you make today to train your soul to desire the Divine Presence more than you desire food?
?
The passage says the sick person's need for food is 'more abundant and more complete' due to bodily weakness. In what area of your life are you spiritually 'sick'—relying too much on physical comforts? How can you begin to transfer that dependence to the Holy Presence?
?
If prolonged abstention from food can be a miracle of spiritual mastery, what does your own relationship with food reveal about the current state of your soul? Are you willing to experience the discomfort of hunger to see if your soul can find stillness in God alone?

The Dream Analogy for Revelation
Taftazani explains revelation via dream analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Taftazani uses the analogy of dreams to explain the possibility of perceiving immaterial angels without physical senses.

Core Idea
Revelation is perceived through internal faculties, not external senses.

Taftazani addresses a philosophical objection: if angels are immaterial, how can they be seen? He offers a rational analogy from everyday experience — dreams — to show that perception through internal faculties is possible. This passage defends the mechanism of revelation by grounding it in a familiar psychological phenomenon.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage once
Read the Arabic and translation to get the overall argument. Notice the structure: a premise about sleepers, then an application to revelation.
This is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the analogy
Taftazani compares revelation to dream experiences. He describes how a sleeper sees and hears things that are not external but exist in the imaginative faculty and common sense.
The key is that these perceptions are real but not physical.
3
Understand 'mujarradāt'
The footnote defines immaterial entities (mujarradāt). Grasp this definition to see why angels, as immaterial, can be perceived without physical bodies.
This concept is central to the argument.
4
Connect to the broader context
Reflect on how this argument defends prophethood and miracles. It shows that revelation does not require physical bodies, only appropriate internal faculties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تقرير هم لنزول الوحي وظهور الملك مع أنه من المجردات (۳) دون الأجسام، فهو أن النائم ومن يجري مجراه في عدم استيلاء الحواس عليه قد يشاهد صوراً غريبة، ويسمع أصواتاً عجيبة ، وليست بمعدومة صرفة ولا موجودة في الخارج، بل في القوة المتخيلة والحس المشترك، وربما لا يكون متأدية إليه من طرق الحواس الظاهرة، بل من عالم آخر، فلا يبعد أن يكون لبعض أفراد الإنسان (۳) المجردات المجرد ما لا يكون محلاً لجوهر ولا حالاً في جوهر آخر ولا مركباً منهما على اصطلاح أهل الحكمة.
As for their establishment for the descent of revelation and the appearance of the angel, despite it being from the immaterial entities (mujarradāt) and not bodies, it is that the sleeper and one in his state of sensory detachment may witness strange images and hear wondrous sounds, and they are neither pure non-existence nor existent externally, but in the imaginative faculty and common sense. And perhaps they do not reach him through the paths of the external senses, but from another world. So it is not far-fetched that some human individuals [might perceive this]. (3) al-Mujarradāt: that which is not a locus for a substance, nor an accident in another substance, nor composed of both, according to the terminology of the philosophers.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage provides a rational explanation for how revelation (waḥy) and the appearance of an angel (zuhūr al-malak) occur, even though angels are immaterial beings (mujarradāt). The author draws an analogy with dream experiences: a sleeper or someone in a state where senses are inactive may see strange images and hear wondrous sounds. These images are not pure non-existence nor external objects; rather, they exist in the imaginative faculty (al-quwwa al-mutakhayyila) and common sense (al-ḥiss al-mushtarak). They may not come through the external senses but from another world (useless? 'ālam ākhar). Thus, it is plausible that some human individuals can perceive angels similarly. The footnote defines mujarradāt as entities that are not a locus for a substance nor an accident in another substance, nor composed of both, i.e., immaterial. The passage thus defends the possibility of prophetic revelation using an analogy with ordinary psychological experiences.

Key Terms
الوحي
الملك
المجردات
القوة المتخيلة
الحس المشترك
عالم آخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels must be physical bodies to be perceived.
Correction: The passage shows that angels, as immaterial entities, can appear in the internal senses (imaginative faculty and common sense) without physical existence, just as dream images are perceived internally.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where do the images seen during revelation exist?
A) In the external world
B) In the imaginative faculty and common sense
C) In the angel's own essence
D) In the sleeper's dreams only

Key Takeaway
Revelation and angelic appearance are possible through internal faculties, as demonstrated by the analogy with dream perception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were in a state of deep sleep and saw a vision of an angel, would you be more likely to dismiss it as a product of your mind or to take it as a genuine communication? What does your answer reveal about your trust in the unseen?
?
The passage shows that revelation comes through faculties that are not dependent on the external world. Are you actively cultivating those faculties through spiritual practice, or are you neglecting them? In the next week, what specific step will you take to become more receptive to divine guidance from within?

The Summary Rebuttal and Non-Arabic Words Objection
Summary rebuttal and first objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the general response to objections against the Quran and the specific objection that it contains non-Arabic words.

Core Idea
The Quran's opponents, despite their eloquence, only called it magic.

The author begins by giving a general defense: the Arab chiefs, though intelligent and hostile, acknowledged the Quran's beauty and only attributed it to sorcery. He then starts detailing specific objections, beginning with the claim that the Quran contains non-Arabic words like 'istabraq' and 'sijjil'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author presents the summary rebuttal first.
The summary rebuttal is a powerful point: the Arabs themselves acknowledged the Quran's perfection.
2
Identify the summary rebuttal
Find the sentence that describes how the Arab chiefs responded to the Quran. What did they say about it?
They called it sorcery due to its perfect beauty.
3
Identify the first objection
Locate the objection about non-Arabic words. What are the two examples given?
The words 'istabraq' and 'sijjil' are mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومشتمل على العلوم والحقائق، وكثير من السور خال عن الإخبار عن المغيبات ووجه دفع المطاعن إجمالاً أن رؤساء العرب مع حذاقتهم وعداوتهم اعترفوا به وأذعنوا ولم يطعنوا بل نسبوه لكمال حسنه إلى السحر وتفصيلاً الجواب عما يورده بعض المعاندين من أعداء الدين مثل ان فيه غير العربي كالاستبرق والسجيل، فكيف يكون عربياً مبيناً، وأن فيه خطأ من جهة الإعراب، مثل: ﴿ إِنَّ هَذَانِ لَسَاحِرَانِ ﴾ وأن فيه مقدار احدى عشرة آية من كلام البشر وهي رَبِّ اشْرَحْ لي صَدْرِي . . الآيات فكيف يصح التحدي بسورة وأقلها ثلاث آيات وأن فيه ما يتمسك به أهل الغواية مثل : الرَّحمنُ عَلَى العَرْشِ اسْتَوى وأن فيه عيب التكرار كقصة فرعون و فَبأي آلاءِ رَبِّكُمَا تُكَذِّبَانِ و وَيل يَوْمَئِذٍ للمكذبين وأن فيه اختلافاً كثيراً من القراءات فكيف يصح قوله ولو كَانَ مِن عِندِ غَيرِ اللَّهِ لَوَجَدُوا فِيهِ اختلافاً كَثِيراً وأن فيه التناقض مثل فيومَئِذٍ لَا يُسْأَلُ عَن ذَنبِهِ إِنْسٌ قبلهم ولا جَانٌ مع قوله فورَبِّكَ لَنَسْأَلَنَّهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ والكذب المحض مثل ولَقَد خَلَقنَاكُم ثُمَّ صَوَّرَنَاكُم ثمَّ قُلْنَا لَلمَلائِكَةِ اسْجُدُوا لآدَمَ . والشعر من كل بحر مثل قوله فمن شاء فليؤمن ومن شاء فليكفر.
And it (the Quran) contains sciences and truths, and many surahs lack reports of the unseen. And the way to repel objections in summary is that the chiefs of the Arabs, despite their intelligence and enmity, acknowledged it and submitted and did not criticize it, but rather attributed it due to its perfect beauty to sorcery. And in detail, the answer to what some obstinate enemies of religion raise, such as that it contains non-Arabic like 'istabraq' and 'sijjil', so how can it be a clear Arabic [Quran]? And that it contains a grammatical error like 'Inna hathani lasahirani'. And that it contains about eleven verses of human speech, which are 'Rabbi ishrah li sadri...' verses. So how can the challenge be valid with a surah, the shortest of which is three verses? And that it contains what the people of misguidance cling to, like 'Al-Rahmanu 'ala al-arshi istawa'. And that it contains the defect of repetition, like the story of Pharaoh and 'Fabi-ayyi ala'i rabbikuma tukadhdhiban' and 'Waylun yawma'idhin lil-mukadhdhibin'. And that it contains much variation in recitations, so how is His statement correct: 'If it had been from other than Allah, they would have found in it much discrepancy'? And that it contains contradiction, like 'Fayawma'idhin la yus'alu 'an dhanbihi insun qablahum wa la jann' along with His statement 'Fawarabbika lanas'alannahum ajma'in'. And plain falsehood, like 'Walaqad khalaqnakum thumma sawwarnakum thumma qulna lil-mala'ikati usjudu li-adama'. And poetry of every meter, like His statement 'Faman sha'a falyu'min waman sha'a falyakfur'.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of objections raised against the Quran by its opponents. The author first gives a general response: the Arab chiefs, despite their eloquence and hostility, acknowledged the Quran and only called it magic. Then he details the specific objections: presence of non-Arabic words like 'istabraq' and 'sijjil', alleged grammatical errors like 'inna hathani lasahirani', inclusion of human speech like 'Rabbi ishrah li sadri', challenge to produce a surah when some verses are long, anthropomorphic verses like 'al-Rahmanu 'ala al-arshi istawa', repetition of stories like that of Pharaoh and refrains, variant readings, contradictions between verses about questioning, and alleged falsehoods like the creation and command to prostrate. The list ends with the objection that some verses are like poetry.

Key Terms
المطاعن
السحر
الاستبرق
السجيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the chiefs of the Arabs say about the Quran?
A) They denied it completely
B) They called it sorcery
C) They said it was poetry
D) They accepted it as divine

Key Takeaway
The Arab chiefs acknowledged the Quran's perfection by calling it magic, not by denying its beauty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Arab chiefs, despite their intelligence, called the Quran 'magic' to avoid submitting to its truth. When you face a clear truth that challenges your pride or lifestyle, do you find excuses like 'it's just not for me' or 'it's too hard'? What false labels are you using to escape the Quran's call?
?
The objection about 'istabraq' and 'sijjil' seems petty—focusing on trivial loanwords to avoid the bigger issue. In your own life, do you ever fixate on minor imperfections in Islam or its followers to avoid fully committing to its message?
?
The Arab chiefs acknowledged the Quran's beauty but still rejected it. You have read this lesson and know it is from Allah. What concrete step will you take today to let the Quran's beauty change something about your daily practice—not just admire it from a distance?

Objections of Grammatical Error and Human Speech Inclusion
Two specific objections: grammar and human speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two objections: an alleged grammatical error in the Quran and the claim that it includes verses from human speakers.

Core Idea
Opponents claim Quran has grammatical mistakes and human speech, challenging its divine origin.

The author lists the next two objections: a supposed grammatical mistake in the verse 'Inna hathani lasahirani' and the claim that some verses, like 'Rabbi ishrah li sadri', are human words. These objections attempt to undermine the Quran's linguistic perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two distinct objections presented.
The grammatical error objection is about the verse 'Inna hathani lasahirani'.
2
Analyze the grammatical objection
What is the alleged error? The verse uses 'hathani' (nominative) after 'inna', which normally requires accusative. Opponents claim this is a mistake.
Scholars explain this as a rare but valid reading or a dialectal variation.
3
Analyze the human speech objection
The second objection claims that verses like 'Rabbi ishrah li sadri' are human prayers, not divine speech. If so, how can the Quran be a challenge?
Muslims respond that quoting human speech in the Quran does not make it less divine.

Which verse is cited as an alleged grammatical error?
A) رَبِّ اشْرَحْ لي صَدْرِي
B) إِنَّ هَذَانِ لَسَاحِرَانِ
C) الرَّحمنُ عَلَى العَرْشِ اسْتَوى
D) فبأي آلاء ربكما تكذبان

Key Takeaway
Two objections claim linguistic flaws: a grammatical variant and the inclusion of human speech, but these are not real defects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the objection that the Quran contains 'human speech' like the prayer of Prophet Musa (AS), do you feel any doubt about the Quran's divine authorship? If so, what is the root of that doubt, and how can this lesson's principle—that the Quran quotes others without losing its divine nature—address it? Commit to memorizing one verse from the Quran that is a quote from a prophet and reflect on why it is still divine.
?
Allegations of grammatical errors in the Quran often feel unsettling. Have you ever encountered such a claim and felt unable to defend the Quran? Based on this lesson, what specific knowledge (e.g., variant readings) do you need to acquire to respond with confidence? Write down one step you will take this week to strengthen your defense of the Quran's linguistic perfection.

Objections of Anthropomorphism, Repetition, and Variant Readings
Three objections: anthropomorphism, repetition, variant readings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three objections: anthropomorphic verses, repetitive stories, and variant Quranic readings.

Core Idea
Critics cite verses like 'al-Rahmanu 'ala al-arshi istawa' to claim anthropomorphism and point to repetitions and variant readings as flaws.

The author now presents three more objections: the verse about Allah's 'istawa' (establishing on the Throne) is seen as anthropomorphism; the repetition of stories like Pharaoh's and refrains like 'Fabi-ayyi ala'i...' are considered defects; and the existence of multiple readings is claimed to contradict the verse denying discrepancy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify three separate objections.
The objection about 'al-Rahmanu 'ala al-arshi istawa' is the first.
2
Understand the anthropomorphism objection
Opponents take 'istawa' literally as physical seating, implying a body. This is a misinterpretation.
Muslims interpret 'istawa' as a state of sovereignty, not physical sitting.
3
Examine the repetition and variant readings objections
Repetition of stories and refrains is seen as redundancy. Variant readings (qira'at) are seen as discrepancies contradicting the verse 'If it were from other than Allah, they would have found much discrepancy'.
Muslims see repetition for emphasis and the qira'at as divinely revealed variations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومشتمل على العلوم والحقائق، وكثير من السور خال عن الإخبار عن المغيبات ووجه دفع المطاعن إجمالاً أن رؤساء العرب مع حذاقتهم وعداوتهم اعترفوا به وأذعنوا ولم يطعنوا بل نسبوه لكمال حسنه إلى السحر وتفصيلاً الجواب عما يورده بعض المعاندين من أعداء الدين مثل ان فيه غير العربي كالاستبرق والسجيل، فكيف يكون عربياً مبيناً، وأن فيه خطأ من جهة الإعراب، مثل: ﴿ إِنَّ هَذَانِ لَسَاحِرَانِ ﴾ وأن فيه مقدار احدى عشرة آية من كلام البشر وهي رَبِّ اشْرَحْ لي صَدْرِي . . الآيات فكيف يصح التحدي بسورة وأقلها ثلاث آيات وأن فيه ما يتمسك به أهل الغواية مثل : الرَّحمنُ عَلَى العَرْشِ اسْتَوى وأن فيه عيب التكرار كقصة فرعون و فَبأي آلاءِ رَبِّكُمَا تُكَذِّبَانِ و وَيل يَوْمَئِذٍ للمكذبين وأن فيه اختلافاً كثيراً من القراءات فكيف يصح قوله ولو كَانَ مِن عِندِ غَيرِ اللَّهِ لَوَجَدُوا فِيهِ اختلافاً كَثِيراً وأن فيه التناقض مثل فيومَئِذٍ لَا يُسْأَلُ عَن ذَنبِهِ إِنْسٌ قبلهم ولا جَانٌ مع قوله فورَبِّكَ لَنَسْأَلَنَّهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ والكذب المحض مثل ولَقَد خَلَقنَاكُم ثُمَّ صَوَّرَنَاكُم ثمَّ قُلْنَا لَلمَلائِكَةِ اسْجُدُوا لآدَمَ . والشعر من كل بحر مثل قوله فمن شاء فليؤمن ومن شاء فليكفر.
And it (the Quran) contains sciences and truths, and many surahs lack reports of the unseen. And the way to repel objections in summary is that the chiefs of the Arabs, despite their intelligence and enmity, acknowledged it and submitted and did not criticize it, but rather attributed it due to its perfect beauty to sorcery. And in detail, the answer to what some obstinate enemies of religion raise, such as that it contains non-Arabic like 'istabraq' and 'sijjil', so how can it be a clear Arabic [Quran]? And that it contains a grammatical error like 'Inna hathani lasahirani'. And that it contains about eleven verses of human speech, which are 'Rabbi ishrah li sadri...' verses. So how can the challenge be valid with a surah, the shortest of which is three verses? And that it contains what the people of misguidance cling to, like 'Al-Rahmanu 'ala al-arshi istawa'. And that it contains the defect of repetition, like the story of Pharaoh and 'Fabi-ayyi ala'i rabbikuma tukadhdhiban' and 'Waylun yawma'idhin lil-mukadhdhibin'. And that it contains much variation in recitations, so how is His statement correct: 'If it had been from other than Allah, they would have found in it much discrepancy'? And that it contains contradiction, like 'Fayawma'idhin la yus'alu 'an dhanbihi insun qablahum wa la jann' along with His statement 'Fawarabbika lanas'alannahum ajma'in'. And plain falsehood, like 'Walaqad khalaqnakum thumma sawwarnakum thumma qulna lil-mala'ikati usjudu li-adama'. And poetry of every meter, like His statement 'Faman sha'a falyu'min waman sha'a falyakfur'.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of objections raised against the Quran by its opponents. The author first gives a general response: the Arab chiefs, despite their eloquence and hostility, acknowledged the Quran and only called it magic. Then he details the specific objections: presence of non-Arabic words like 'istabraq' and 'sijjil', alleged grammatical errors like 'inna hathani lasahirani', inclusion of human speech like 'Rabbi ishrah li sadri', challenge to produce a surah when some verses are long, anthropomorphic verses like 'al-Rahmanu 'ala al-arshi istawa', repetition of stories like that of Pharaoh and refrains, variant readings, contradictions between verses about questioning, and alleged falsehoods like the creation and command to prostrate. The list ends with the objection that some verses are like poetry.

ويل يومئذ للمكذبين

Three distinct objections are raised: anthropomorphic interpretability, narrative repetition, and variation in readings.

?
If someone told you that variant readings prove the Quran has been changed, would you be able to respond with confidence? What single verse from this lesson can you memorize today to fortify your heart against such doubt?

Objections of Contradiction, Falsehood, and Poetry
Final three objections: contradiction, falsehood, poetry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the final three objections: alleged contradictions, false statements, and poetic verses.

Core Idea
Opponents claim the Quran contradicts itself, contains falsehoods like the creation order, and is poetry.

The author concludes the list of objections with three more: an apparent contradiction between verses about questioning, an alleged falsehood in the creation sequence, and the claim that some verses are poetry. These objections challenge the Quran's consistency, truthfulness, and literary classification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the three objections: contradiction, falsehood, poetry.
The contradiction involves two verses about questioning on Judgment Day.
2
Analyze the contradiction objection
One verse says 'no one will be asked about their sin', another says 'We will surely question them'. Opponents see this as contradictory.
Scholars reconcile by saying questioning is for confirmation, not information.
3
Examine the falsehood and poetry objections
The falsehood objection points to the sequence: 'We created you, then formed you, then said to angels: prostrate to Adam' – but Adam was not present at creation. The poetry objection cites 'Faman sha'a falyu'min...' as being in poetic meter.
Muslims explain the creation verse as a summary, and poetic rhythm does not invalidate divine origin.
